1 Scope 1 
This Technical Specification has been produced by the O-RAN Alliance. 2 
The contents of the present document are subject to continuing work within O-RAN and may change following formal 3 
O-RAN approval. Should the O-RAN Alliance modify the contents of the present document, it will be re-released by O-4 
RAN with an identifying change of release date and an increase in version number as follows:  5 
Release x.y.z 6 
where: 7 
x the first digit is incremented for all changes of substance, i.e. technical enhancements, corrections, updates, 8 
etc. (the initial approved document will have x=01). 9 
y the second digit is incremented when editorial only changes have been incorporated in the document.  10 
z the third digit included only in working versions of the document indicating incremental changes during the 11 
editing process. 12 
The present document specifies the E2 Service Model (E2SM) for the Near RT RIC RAN Control interaction.  13

3 Definitions and Abbreviations 1 
3.1 Definitions 2 
E2 Node: as defined in E2GAP [2].  3 
RAN Function: as defined in E2GAP [2] 4 
E2 Service Model: The description of the Services exposed by a specific RAN function within an E2 node over the E2 5 
interface towards the Near-RT RIC. 6 
3.2 Abbreviations 7 
For the purposes of the present document, the following abbreviations apply.  8 
O-CU  O- RAN Central Unit 9 
O-CU-CP O- RAN Central Unit – Control Plane 10 
O-CU-UP O- RAN Central Unit – User Plane 11 
O-DU O- RAN Distributed Unit   12 
Near-RT RIC Near-real-time RAN Intelligent Controller 13 
RC RAN Control 14

ORAN.WG3.E2SM-RC-v01.00

4 General 1 
4.1 Procedure Specification Principles 2 
The principle for specifying the procedure logic is to specify the functional behaviour of the terminating node exactly 3 
and completely. Any rule that specifies the behaviour of the originating node shall be possible to be verified with 4 
information that is visible within the system. 5 
The following specification principles have been applied for the procedure text in clause 8:  6 
- The procedure text discriminates between: 7 
1) Functionality which "shall" be executed. 8 
 The procedure text indicates that the receiving node "shall" perform a certain function Y under a certain 9 
condition. If the receiving node supports procedure X but cannot perform functionality Y requested in the 10 
REQUEST message of a Class 1 EP, the receiving node shall respond with the message used to report 11 
unsuccessful outcome for this procedure, containing an appropriate cause value.  12 
2) Functionality which "shall, if supported" be executed. 13 
 The procedure text indicates that the receiving node "shall, if supported," perform a certain function Y under 14 
a certain condition. If the receiving node supports procedure X, but does not support functionality Y, the 15 
receiving node shall proceed with the execution of the EP, possibly informing the requesting node about the 16 
not supported functionality. 17 
- Any required inclusion of an optional IE in a response message is explicitly indicated in the procedure text. If the 18 
procedure text does not explicitly indicate that an optional IE shall be included in a response message, the 19 
optional IE shall not be included. For requirements on including Criticality Diagnostics IE, see clause 10. 20 
4.2 Forwards and Backwards Compatibility 21 
The forwards and backwards compatibility of the protocol is assured by a mechanism where all current and future 22 
messages, and IEs or groups of related IEs, include ID and criticality fields that are coded in a standard format that will 23 
not be changed in the future. These parts can always be decoded regardless of  the standard version. 24 
4.3 Specification Notations 25 
For the purposes of the present document, the following notations apply: 26 
Service when referring to a Service in the specification the SERVICE NAME is written with upper case 27 
characters and in bold followed by the word "service", e.g. REPORT service. 28 
Procedure When referring to an elementary procedure in the specification the Procedure Name is written with 29 
the first letters in each word in upper case characters followed by the word "procedure", e.g. 30 
Handover Preparation procedure. 31 
Message When referring to a message in the specification the MESSAGE NAME is written with all letters 32 
in upper case characters followed by the word "message", e.g. HANDOVER REQUEST message.  33 
IE When referring to an information element (IE) in the specification the Information Element Name  34 
is written with the first letters in each word in upper case characters and all letters in Italic font 35 
followed by the abbreviation "IE", e.g. E-RAB ID IE. 36 
Value of an IE When referring to the value of an information element (IE) in the specification the "Value" is 37 
written as it is specified in the specification enclosed by quotation marks, e.g. "Value".  38 

ORAN.WG3.E2SM-RC-v01.00

4.4 Identifiers 1 
For the purposes of the present document, the following identifiers are defined: 2 
Style Type The identifier used to nominate a specific approach or Style used to exposing a given RIC Service 3 
(REPORT, INSERT, CONTROL and POLICY).  The same E2SM may support more than one 4 
Style for each RIC Service. 5 
Format Type The identifier used to nominate a specific formatting approach used to encode one of the E2AP IEs 6 
defined in this E2SM.  The same E2SM may support more than one encoding Formats for each 7 
E2AP IE and each E2AP IE message encoding Format may be used by one or more RIC Service 8 
Styles. 9 
  10 

ORAN.WG3.E2SM-RC-v01.00

5 E2SM Services 1 
As defined in E2 General Aspects and Principles [1], a given RAN Function offers a set of services to be exposed over 2 
the E2 (REPORT, INSERT, CONTROL and/or POLICY) using E2AP [3] defined procedures. Each of the E2AP 3 
Procedures listed in table 5-1 contains specific E2 Node RAN Function dependent Information Elements (IEs).  4 
Table 5-1: Relationship RAN Function specific E2AP Information elements and E2AP Procedures  5

6 RAN Function Service Model Description 1 
6.1 RAN Function Overview 2 
For the purposes of this E2 Service Model, E2SM-RC, the E2 Node terminating the E2 Interface is assumed to host one 3 
or more instances of the RAN Function “RAN Control” which performs the following functionalities:  4 
- E2 REPORT services used to expose RAN control and UE context related information 5 
- E2 INSERT services used to suspend RAN control related call processes 6 
- E2 CONTROL services used to resume or initiate RAN control related call processes, modify RAN 7 
configuration and/or E2 service-related UE context information 8 
- E2 POLICY services used to modify the behaviour of RAN control related processes  9 
This E2SM specification provides a set of RAN Function exposure services described in clause 6.2 and has been 10 
prepared with the assumption that the same E2SM may be used to describe either a single RAN Function in the E2 11 
Node handling all RAN control related call processes or more than one RAN Function in the E2 Node with each 12 
instance handling a subset of the RAN control related call processes on the E2 Node. 13 
6.2 RAN Function exposure services 14 
6.2.1 REPORT service 15 
The “RAN Control” RAN Function provides selective support of the following REPORT  services: 16 
- Copy of Complete message (from Network Interface or RRC), used for monitoring POLICY services, data 17 
gathering (to populate the Near-RT RIC UE-NIB and/or ML services data pipeline), etc. 18 
- Call process outcome with associated information on UE context and/or RAN status information, used for 19 
monitoring [CONTROL and] POLICY services, data gathering (to populate the Near-RT RIC UE-NIB and/or 20 
ML services data pipeline), etc.  21 
- E2 Node Information and Cell related Information, used for monitoring of E2 Node and Cell configuration 22 
changes, triggering POLICY deletion, changing notifications (to reset Near-RT RIC optimization services), etc.   23 
- UE Information, used for monitoring of UE information changes, triggering E2 Control, location tracking, etc.  24 
- On Demand Report, used for reporting Cell related, E2 Node related and UE related information to Near -RT RIC 25 
when requested by Near-RT RIC. 26 
NOTE: Only the UE with user consent can be configured to report location information.  27 
6.2.2 INSERT service 28 
The “RAN Control” RAN Function provides selective support of the following INSERT services: 29 
- Radio Bearer Control request, used for requesting the RIC to control DRB QoS modification, QoS flow to DRB 30 
(re)mapping, Logical channel (re)configuration, Radio bearer admission control, Split bearer and PDCP 31 
duplication control, etc. 32 
- Radio Resource Allocation Control request, used for requesting the RIC to control Discontinuous Reception 33 
(DRX), Scheduling request (SR), Semi-Persistent Scheduling (SPS), Configured Grant, Slice level PRB quota, 34 
Channel Quality Indicator (CQI) table, etc. 35 
- Connected Mode Mobility Control request, used for requesting the RIC to control operations of Handover (HO), 36 
Conditional handover (CHO), Dual Active Protocol Stack (DAPS) HO, etc. 37 
- Radio Access Control request, used for requesting the RIC to control parameters related to RACH ba ck-off, 38 
RRC connection reject, RRC connection release, Access barring, UE admission, etc.  39 
- Dual Connectivity (DC) Control request, used for requesting the RIC to control operations of Dual Connectivity 40 
(DC) including Change of bearer termination point (MN or SN) and/or bearer types, etc. 41 

ORAN.WG3.E2SM-RC-v01.00 
 
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN ALLIANCE e.V. Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in the Annex ZZZ 
14 
- Carrier Aggregation (CA) Control request, used for requesting the RIC to control operations of Carrier 1 
Aggregation (CA) involving secondary cell re-selection. 2 
- Idle Mode Mobility Control request, used for requesting the RIC to control intra-frequency, inter-frequency, 3 
inter-RAT cell reselection priority, idle timers, etc. 4 
6.2.3 CONTROL service 5 
The “RAN Control” RAN Function provides selective support of the following CONTROL  services: 6 
- Radio Bearer Control, used for DRB QoS modification, QoS flow to DRB (re)mapping, Logical channel 7 
(re)configuration, Radio bearer admission control, Split bearer and PDCP duplication control, etc. 8 
- Radio Resource Allocation Control, used to control Discontinuous Reception (DRX), Scheduling request (SR), 9 
Semi-Persistent Scheduling (SPS), Configured Grant, Slice level PRB quota, Channel Quality Indicator (CQI) 10 
table, etc. 11 
- Connected Mode Mobility Control, used to control operations of Handover (HO), Conditional handover (CHO), 12 
Dual Active Protocol Stack (DAPS) HO, etc. 13 
- Radio Access Control, used for modification of RACH back-off, RRC connection reject, RRC connection 14 
release, Access barring, UE admission, etc. 15 
- Dual Connectivity (DC) Control, used to control operations of Dual Connectivity (DC) including Change of 16 
bearer termination point (MN or SN) and/or bearer types, etc. 17 
- Carrier Aggregation (CA) Control, used to control operations of Carrier Aggregation (CA). 18 
- Idle Mode Mobility Control, used for modification of intra-frequency, inter-frequency, inter-RAT cell 19 
reselection priority, idle timers, etc.  20 
- UE to RAN UE group assignment, used to support POLICY services. 21 
6.2.4 POLICY service 22 
The “RAN Control” RAN Function provides selective support of the following POLICY services: 23 
- Radio Bearer Policy, used to modify the behaviour of call processes related to DRB QoS control, QoS flow to 24 
DRB mapping, Logical channel configuration, Radio bearer admission control, Split bearer and PDCP 25 
duplication control, etc. 26 
- Radio Resource Allocation Policy, used to modify the behaviour of call processes related to DRX, SR, SPS, 27 
Configured Grant, Slice level PRB quota, CQI table, etc. 28 
- Connected Mode Mobility Policy, used to modify the behaviour of call processes related to HO, CHO, DAPS 29 
HO, etc. for both serving and target RAN nodes. 30 
- Radio Access Policy, used to modify the behaviour of call processes related to RACH back- off, RRC connection 31 
reject, RRC connection release, Access barring, UE admission, etc. 32 
- Dual Connectivity (DC) Policy, used to modify the behaviour of call processes related to DC related operations 33 
for both master and secondary RAN nodes, Change of bearer termination point (MN or SN) and/or bearer types, 34 
etc. 35 
- Carrier Aggregation (CA) Policy, used to modify the behaviour of call processes related to CA related operations 36 
for both primary and secondary cells. 37 
- Idle Mode Mobility Policy, used to modify the behaviour of call processes related to intra -frequency, inter-38 
frequency, inter-RAT cell reselection priority, inactivity timers, etc. 39 
6.3 REPORT service description 40 
The E2SM-RC REPORT service requirements defined in Section 6.2.1 are offered using a set of REPORT Styles.  All 41 
REPORT styles are implemented using a set of IEs for Action Definition, RIC Indication Header and RIC Indication 42 
Message and have specific Event Trigger approach. For each Report style, a single RAN Parameter table is used to 43 
specify the required information to be reported. 44 
The following REPORT styles are supported:  45 

ORAN.WG3.E2SM-RC-v01.00 
 
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN ALLIANCE e.V. Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in the Annex ZZZ 
15 
- Message copy: This REPORT style is initiated by “Message Event” Event Trigger and is used to report complete 1 
NI or RRC message along with UE associated information when the event trigger conditions are satisfied.  2 
- Call Process Outcome: This REPORT style is initiated by the corresponding "Call Process Breakpoint" Event 3 
Trigger and is used to report on the outcome of a call process providing information on current, and in certain 4 
cases previous, UE or E2 Node information depending upon the nature of the target call process.   5 
- E2 Node Information: This REPORT style is initiated by “E2 Node Information Change” Event Trigger and is 6 
used to report cell related and E2 Node related information upon event trigger conditions are satisfied. 7 
- UE information: This REPORT style is initiated by “UE Information Change” Event Trigger and is used to 8 
report UE related information and UE state variables upon the event trigger conditions are satisfied.  9 
- On demand report: This REPORT style is initiated by “On Demand” Event Trigger and is used to report cell -10 
related and UE-related information on an adhoc basis upon request from Near-RT RIC. 11 
6.4 INSERT service description 12 
The E2SM-RC INSERT service requirements defined in Section 6.2.2 are offered using a set of INSERT Styles. Each 13 
style corresponds to a set of “INSERT Indications”, where each “INSERT Indication” deals with a specific functionality  14 
and has a set of associated RAN parameters, provided in a mapping table. All INSERT Service styles are implemented 15 
using a set of IEs that constitute “Action Definition”, “RIC Indication Header” and “RIC Indication Message” to deliver 16 
RAN Control -related INSERT services. Each INSERT service style is associated with a specific “Event Trigger” 17 
approach.  An “INSERT Indication” is used to request the RIC to control a functionality associated with the respective 18 
INSERT service style, and to set or modify the values of one or more associated RAN parameters.  19 
As an example, upon the arrival of an RRC Measurement Report in the E2 node due to the occurrence of an A3 event 20 
pertaining to a UE (which constitutes the event trigger), the E2 node can send a message to the RIC using the “Connected 21 
Mode Mobility” INSERT service style and the “Handover Control Request” INSERT Indication along with the “target 22 
cell ID” parameter. This RIC should then accept/deny the “Handover Control Request”, and if it accepts, it should set the 23 
value of the “target cell ID” parameter and send a CONTROL action back to the RIC. Up until then, the E2 node suspends 24 
the ongoing call processing for the UE.  25 
6.5 CONTROL service description 26 
The E2SM-RC CONTROL service requirements defined in Section 6.2.3 are offered using a set of CONTROL Styles. 27 
Each style corresponds to a set of “CONTROL Action”, where each “CONTROL Action” deals with a specific 28 
functionality and has a set of associated RAN parameters, provided in a mapping table. All CONTROL Service styles are 29 
implemented using a set of IEs constituting a “RIC Control Request Header” and a “RIC Control Request Message” to 30 
deliver RAN Control-related CONTROL services. A “CONTROL Action” containing one or more RAN parameters and 31 
their associated values can either be sent from the RIC, either asynchronously to the E2 node or as a response to a previous 32 
“INSERT Indication” from the E2 node.  33 
Referring to the previous example in Section 6.4, the RIC sends a “CONTROL action” that accepts/denies the incom ing 34 
“INSERT Indication” requesting for “Handover Control”, along with the value of the “Target Primary Cell”. As another 35 
example, the RIC can also asynchronously send a “CONTROL action” asking the E2 node to configure the UE in Carrier 36 
Aggregation mode and  setup one or more secondary cells to the UE, whose values are assigned by the RIC via the 37 
“CONTROL action”. 38 
6.6 POLICY service description 39 
6.6.1 Overview 40 
The E2SM-RC POLICY service requirements defined in Section 6.2.4 are offered using a set of POLICY Styles.  Each 41 
style is implemented using multiple "Policy Approach" strategies, each with a specific methodology defined to use the 42 
E2AP IE "Action Definition" to deliver RAN Control related POLICY services.  43 
The following Policy Approaches are defined: 44 

ORAN.WG3.E2SM-RC-v01.00 
 
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN ALLIANCE e.V. Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in the Annex ZZZ 
16 
- Control: POLICY for a given Style and Action ID is defined as a single case of a specific Policy condition with 1 
the corresponding Policy Action defined using the same data structure as CONTROL which would be used to 2 
replace default RAN behaviour. 3 
- Offset: POLICY for a given Style and Action ID is defined as a set of different cases applicable for a range of 4 
different Policy conditions with the corresponding Policy Action defined using the dedicated data structure 5 
defined for POLICY which would be used to modify default RAN behaviour. 6 
6.6.2 Policy approach "Control" 7 
The “control” Policy Approach is similar to the CONTROL service, with static conditions and actions in the RIC 8 
Subscription used to select an appropriate CONTROL Action. When a set of Policy conditi ons are satisfied, then E2 9 
Node is instructed to execute a Policy Action with a set of supplementary or default set of RAN parameters.  10 
A single Policy Action shall be a result of execution of multiple policy conditions.  11 
- Each Policy Condition is defined using a combination of RAN Parameters and conditional tests associated with 12 
UE and Call process related information. 13 
- Each Policy Action is defined with a single Policy Action ID (command) which instructs E2 Node to perform a 14 
certain action when the conditions are satisfied. The Policy Action ID shall be supplemented with a set of RAN 15 
Parameters which may be used to provide information on default values to E2 Node.  16 
Examples include: 17 
- Connected mode mobility policy, Handover Execution: Message Arrival breakpoint event trigger is defined to 18 
initiate the Policy service. On the arrival of A3 Measurement Report, the Policy service kicks in. Policy service 19 
installs a set of Policy Conditions like RSRP > ‘x’ db + Target Node Load < ‘x’ value + Number of successful 20 
HO to target Node > ‘x’ value. When these Policy conditions are satisfied, then perform Policy Action -  21 
“Execute HO” defined in the CONTROL service in Section 6.5. The Policy Action may be provided as a 22 
standalone Policy Action ID “Execute HO” without any RAN parameters. As an alternative, Policy Action 23 
“Execute HO” may be supplemented with default RAN parameters like Handover only QCI 5 and 9 bearers.  24 
- Carrier Aggregation Policy, CA Release decision: A call process breakpoint event trigger is defined t o initiate 25 
the POLICY service. The call process breakpoint shall define conditions for Buffer occupancy. A call process 26 
breakpoint event shall be triggered when the Buffer Occupancy (BO) < ‘x’ KB. In this scenario, the event trigger 27 
satisfies the Policy condition. Hence there is no need to define a Policy condition in the Policy service, When the 28 
BO < ‘x’ KB kicks in, then Policy Action shall instruct E2 Node to “Release Scell” . 29 
6.6.3 Policy Approach "Offset" 30 
The "offset" Policy Approach is based on the design assumption that the Policy Action IE is used to carry one or more 31 
RAN Parameters that are used to modify default E2 Node behaviour via the addition of an "offset" to be applied to 32 
given target threshold or other parameter used in the target call process.   33 
The applicable Policy Action is dependent upon a set of Policy Conditions and a given POLICY service may support 34 
one or more Policy conditions and so provide a targeted Policy Action for a range of diffe rent specific cases, each 35 
defined using a unique Policy condition where: 36 
- Each Policy Condition is defined using a combination of RAN Parameters and conditional tests associated with 37 
UE and Call process related information.  The first positive match in a list of Policy conditions is used to select 38 
the corresponding Policy Action. 39 
- Each Policy Action is defined using a list of RAN Parameters of data type INTEGER or REAL which may to 40 
used directly for default values of type INTEGER or REAL (i.e. Default+Off set) and indirectly to for default 41 
values of type ENUMERATED (i.e. select value in list that is Offset before or after default value).   42 
Examples include: 43 
- Connected mode mobility policy, Handover decision: A call process breakpoint event trigger is defined to 44 
initiate the POLICY service from within the call process handling UE measurement reports related to handover 45 
decisions for a specific target Slice and primary cell currently subject to Traffic Steering guidance.  The Policy 46 
conditions list of RAN Parameters supports the definition of different A3 measurement threshold criteria offset 47 
values to be applied to UEs with a specific combination of slice ID, active QoS bearers, velocity and throughput 48 

ORAN.WG3.E2SM-RC-v01.00 
 
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN ALLIANCE e.V. Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in the Annex ZZZ 
17 
and subject to overall E2 Node load and cell level load balancing requirements.  Handover is accepted if the 1 
reported A3 measurement is greater than the default A3 measurement threshold+offset.  2 
- Carrier Aggregation Policy, CA release decision: A call process breakpoint event trigger is defined to initiate the 3 
POLICY service from within the call process related to Carrier Aggregation (CA) release decisions for a specific 4 
target Slice currently subject to QoE guidance.  The Policy conditions list of RAN Parameters supports the 5 
definition of different CA release threshold criteria offset values to be applied to UEs with a specific 6 
combination of slice ID, active QoS bearers, velocity and throughput and subject to overall E2 Node load and 7 
cell level load balancing requirements.  CA release is initiated if the UE thro ughput is less than the default UE 8 
throughput threshold+offset. 9

- Event trigger styles list along with the corresponding encoding type for each associated E2AP IE.  15 
- RIC REPORT Service styles list along with the corresponding encoding type for each associated E2AP IE.  16 
- RIC INSERT Service styles list along with the corresponding encoding type for each associated E2AP IE.  17 
- RIC CONTROL Service styles list along with the corresponding encoding type for each associated E2AP IE.  18 
- RIC POLICY Service styles list along with the corresponding encoding type for each associated E2AP IE.  19

7.3.2 RIC Event trigger definition IE style 1: Message Event 1 
This RIC Event Trigger Definition IE style is used to detect a specific Network Interface or RRC message event in E2 2 
Node. The dection can be based on only for incoming or outgoing message. The E2 Node can also be configured to 3 
detect multiple messages simultaneously and to trigger only when all the configured message events happen or for any 4 
logical combination of message events.  5 
Each message event configured can be further conditioned to be associated only for a certain UE or group of UEs as 6 
indicated by the Associated UE Info IE if included, or only for some specific UE events defined in Section 8.1.5 as 7 
indicated by the Associated UE Event IE if included. In case that the Global Associated UE Info IE is included, the 8 
information is applied uniformly to all the message events configured and the IE shall override any Associated UE Info 9 
IE included for some message events. 10 
For each message event configured, Event Trigger Condition ID is assigned so that E2 Node can reply to Near -RT RIC 11 
in the RIC INDICATION message to inform which event(s) are the cause for triggering. 12 
This RIC Event Trigger Definition IE style uses RIC Event Trigger Definition IE Format 1 (9.2.1.1.1). 13

conditioned to be associated with a certain E2 Node related information.  17

- UE identifier change (based on UE ID defined in Section 9.3.10)  3

and 8.1.1.8) 5

7.3.6 RIC Event trigger definition IE style 5: On Demand 13 
This RIC Event Trigger Definition IE style is used to be immediately triggered by E2 Node when a RIC subscription 14 
having this event trigger is accepted. Once accepted, the E2 Node shall consider that this RIC subscription shall expire 15 
automatically once all the requested actions for this RIC subscription are performed by the E2 Node.  16 
The event can be further conditioned to be associated only for a certain UE or group of UEs as indicated by the 17 
Associated UE Info IE if included, or for a specific cell or group of cells as indicated by the Associated Cell Info IE if 18 
included. In this case, Near-RT RIC shall ensure that additional conditions imposed by the Associated UE Info IE or 19 
Associated Cell Info IE does not prevent event triggering as soon as the RIC subscription is accepted by the E2 Node. 20 
This RIC Event Trigger Definition IE style uses the RIC Event Trigger Definition IE Format 5 (9.2.1.1.5). 21

7.4 Supported RIC REPORT Services 23 
7.4.1 REPORT Service style list 24 
RIC Style Type Style Name Style Description 
1 Message copy This style is used to report a copy of complete Network Interface or 
RRC message. 
2 Call Process Outcome This style is used to report the outcome of an ongoing call process. 
3 E2 Node Information This style is used to report E2 Node information, Serving Cell 
Configuration and Neighbour Relation related information. 
4 UE Information This style is used to report the UE related information like PDCP, 
RLC, MAC UE state variables and RRC UE State. 
5 On Demand Report This style is used to report snapshot of UE related information and 
Cell related information upon request from Near-RT RIC.

7.4.2 REPORT Service Style 1: Message Copy 1 
7.4.2.1 REPORT Service Style description 2 
This REPORT Service style provides the complete copy of a Network Interface or RRC message to be carried as a 3 
transparent container in the RIC Indication Message IE. 4 
This REPORT service style may also be used to report UE specific information associated with the Network 5 
Interface/RRC messages as provided in Section 8.2.1 RAN Parameters. Examples include reporting of UEID to Near -6 
RT RIC when UE attaches to the E2 Node or when the UEID changes during Xn Handover, UE events like Secon dary 7 
Cell addition, Arrival of A3 Measurement Report (see Section 8.1.5 for the list of UE events).  8 
This REPORT Service style is initiated by Event Trigger style 1: Message Event . 9 
7.4.2.2 REPORT Service RIC Action Definition IE contents 10 
The Action Definition for this service style is used to request E2 Node to report a copy of NI and/or RRC message and 11 
may be used to report UE specific information. The action definition indicates which related UE information is to be 12 
reported along with the NI or RRC message that triggers this report service. 13 
This REPORT Service style uses the RIC Action Definition IE Format 1 (9.2.1.2.1). The supported Parameters for this 14 
format are provided in Section 8.2.1. 15 
7.4.2.3 REPORT Service RIC Indication Header IE contents 16 
This REPORT Service style uses the RIC Indication Header IE Format 1 (9.2.1.3.1) 17 
7.4.2.4 REPORT Service RIC Indication Message IE contents 18 
The REPORT Service RIC Indication Message IE carries the complete Network Interface or RRC message as 19 
transparent containers. The RIC Indication Message IE may also carry UE specific information related to the Network 20 
Interface or RRC message as provided in Section 8.2.1. 21 
This REPORT Service style uses the RIC Indication Message IE Format 1 (9.2.1.4.1). The supported Parameters for 22 
this message format are provided in Section 8.2.1. 23 
7.4.3 REPORT Service Style 2: Call Process Outcome 24 
7.4.3.1 REPORT Service Style description 25 
This REPORT Service style provides the outcome of a target call process related mechanism to be carried in the RIC 26 
Indication Message IE along with an associated RIC Indication Header IE providing information related event trigger 27 
conditions.  28 
This REPORT Service style is initiated by Event Trigger style 2: Call Process Breakpoint. 29 
7.4.3.2 REPORT Service RIC Action Definition IE contents 30 
The Action Definition for this service style is used to request an E2 Node to report call process outcome information 31 
including UE specific information. The Action Definition indicates which related UE information is to be reported 32 
related to the outcome of the event that triggers this report service. 33 
This REPORT Service style uses the RIC Action Definition IE Format 1 (9.2.1.2.1). The supported Par ameters for this 34 
message format are provided in Section 8.2.2. 35 
7.4.3.3 REPORT Service RIC Indication Header IE contents 36 
This REPORT Service style uses the RIC Indication Header IE Format 1 (9.2.1.3.1). 37

7.4.4 REPORT Service S tyle 3: E2 Node Information.   6 
7.4.4.1 REPORT Service Style description 7

provided by E2AP [3]. The information is carried in the RIC Indication Message IE along with an associated RIC 9 
Indication Header IE providing information related event trigger conditions. The required information to be provided is 10 
controlled using the associated RIC Action Definition IE parameters. 11 
This REPORT Service style provides information related to: 12 
- Serving Cell configuration 13 
- Neighbour Relation Information  14 
whenever the corresponding event trigger for change in information content is satisfied. With every change in the 15 
information content of the Neighbour Relation Information, complete list of Neighbour relation table is sent to Near -RT 16 
RIC with indicaton on the modified information. 17 
This REPORT Service style is initiated by Event Trigger style 3: E2 Node Information Change . 18

7.4.6 REPORT Service Style 5: On Demand Report 22 
7.4.6.1 REPORT Service Style description 23 
This REPORT Service style provides the snapshot of the following information at the time of subscripti on request 24 
received from Near-RT RIC:  25 
- Cell Configuration related information  26 
- Neighbour Relation related information 27 
- UE Context related information 28 
The subscription for this REPORT Service style expires once the RIC Indication message is sent with the requested 29 
information. The E2AP RIC Subscription Delete procedure or RIC Subscription Delete Required procedure [3] is not 30 
required to delete this subscription. The reporting shall be per UE based or per cell based depending on the information 31 
requested to be reported. 32

Near-RT RIC.  35

format are provided in Section 8.2.5. 37

RIC Style 
Type 
Style Name Style Description 
1 Radio Bearer Control Request Used to request modification of the configuration of Radio Bearer 
Control (RBC) related parameters. 
2 Radio Resource Allocation 
Control Request 
Used to request modification of the configuration of Radio 
Resource Allocation control related parameters. 
3 Connected Mode Mobility 
Control Request 
Used to request initiation of a connected mode mobility procedure 
(Handover or Conditional Handover), optionally with Dual Active 
Protocol Stack (DAPS), for a specific UE towards either a target 
cell (for HO) or a list of candidate cells (for CHO)

controlling UE access to cells

Request 
Used to request initiation of dual connectivity (DC) mechanisms

Request 
Used to request initiation of carrier aggregation (CA) mechanisms

Request 
Used to request modification of idle mode mobility related functions 
in order to control UE re-selection of cells

7.5.2 INSERT Service Style 1: Radio Bearer Control Request 13 
7.5.2.1 INSERT Service Style description 14 
This INSERT Service style provides a mechanism to initiate request to the RIC for controlling the functionalities of a 15 
radio bearer related process pertaining to a UE using the RIC Indication Message IE and associated RIC Indication Header 16 
IE. The E2 node sends a RIC Indication message to the near-RT RIC and the ongoing call process is suspended at the E2 17 
node until the E2 node hears back from the RIC. The optional RIC Call Process ID  IE is used by the E2 node to match a 18 
RIC Control Request message to a RIC Insert Indication message, following which the E2 node can resume the suspended 19 
call processing for the UE.   20 
Applications of this service include: 21 
- Request for DRB QoS Modification, to tune DRB level QoS related parameters to meet the QoS optimization 22 
targets. 23 
- Request for QoS Flow (re)mapping, to adjust the mapping relationship between QoS flows and DRBs.  24 
- Request for Logical channel (re)configuration 25 
- Request for Radio Bearer Admission Control, to configure DRB admission control such as reject or release may 26 
be applied. 27 
- Request for Split bearer and PDCP duplication control 28 

ORAN.WG3.E2SM-RC-v01.00

request raised by the E2 node and to accordingly set the values for the associated RAN parameters by the RIC via the 6 
control action in the ensuing RIC Control Request message from the RIC. 7

using the RIC Indication Message  IE and asso ciated RIC Indication Header IE. The E2 node sends a RIC Indication 8 
message to the near-RT RIC and the ongoing call process is suspended at the E2 node until the E2 node hears back from 9 
the RIC. The optional RIC Call Process ID IE is used by the E2 node to match a RIC Control Request message to a RIC 10 
Insert Indication message, following which the E2 node can resume the suspended call processing for the UE . 11 
Applications of this service include: 12 
- Request for Carrier Aggregation (CA) initiation for a selected UE towards a target secondary cell or cells 13 
- Request for Carrier Aggregation (CA) modification for a selected UE, or Secondary cell change for a selected UE 14 
towards a target secondary cell or cells 15 
- Request for Carrier Aggregation (CA) release initiation for a selected UE 16 
7.5.7.2 INSERT Service RIC Action Definition IE contents 17 
This INSERT Service style uses the RIC Action Definition  IE Format 3  (9.2.1.2.3). The Insert style deals with the 18 
following Indication services, each service listed below with a corresponding Indication ID. The RAN parameters, 19 
associated with each Insert Indication service, are listed in the sections shown below, and are included by the E2 node in 20 
the RIC Indication message. Via the RIC Indication message, the E2 node seeks the near -RT RIC to accept or deny the 21 
request raised by the E2 node and to accordingly, set the values for the associated RAN parameters by the RIC via the 22 
control action in the ensuing RIC Control Request message from the RIC. 23

7.6 Supported RIC CONTROL Services 1 
7.6.1 CONTROL Service Style Types 2 
RIC Style Type Style Name Style Description 
1 Radio Bearer control Used to modify the configuration the Radio Bearer Control (RBC) 
related parameters and/or behaviours at the E2 Node for a 
specific UE 
2 Radio resource allocation 
control 
Used to modify the configuration the Radio Resource Allocation 
control related parameters and/or behaviours at the E2 Node for a 
specific E2 Node, cell, slice, UE and/or QoS 
3 Connected mode mobility 
control  
Used to initiate a connected mode mobility procedure (Handover 
or Conditional Handover), optionally with Dual Active Protocol 
Stack (DAPS), for a specific UE towards either a target cell (for 
HO) or a list of candidate cells (for CHO) 
4 Radio access control Used to modify Radio access related functions used to control UE 
access to cells 
5 Dual connectivity (DC) control Used to initiate Dual connectivity (DC) mechanisms 
6 Carrier Aggregation (CA) 
control 
Used to initiate Carrier Aggregation (CA) mechanisms 
7 Idle mode mobility control Used to modify Idle mode mobility related functions used to control 
UE reselection of cells 
8 UE information and 
assignment 
Used for Explicit UE list assignment, UE information report 
generation and to complete UE identification.  These services are 
used to support other RIC services. 
 3 
Each of the Control Service Styles 1-8 listed above points to adopt the following common features: 4 
• Control Action ID: The index ID for the individual control action under a given Control Service style.  5 
• Control Action Name: Indicates the functionality of the E2 node which is controlled by Near -RT RIC 6 
• Control Action Description: Describes the control action and functionality of the receiving E2 Node.  7 
• Associated RAN parameters: Identifies the RAN parameters to be controlled by Near -RT RIC pertaining to the 8 
given control action. 9 
The details of the individual Control Service Styles are provided in subsequent sections. 10 
7.6.2 CONTROL Service Style 1: Radio Bearer Control 11 
7.6.2.1 CONTROL Service Style description 12 
This CONTROL Service style provides a mechanism to initiate or resume a radio bearer control related process using 13 
the RIC Control Message IE and associated RIC Control Header IE and the optional RIC Call Process ID  IE used when 14 
resuming a call process following a previous INSERT service . The corresponding INSERT service is service style 1 15 
covered in Section 7.5.2.   16 
Applications of this service include: 17 
- DRB QoS Modification, to tune DRB level QoS related parameters to meet the QoS optimization targets.  18 
- QoS Flow (re)mapping, to adjust the mapping relationship between QoS flows and DRBs.  19 
- Logical channel (re)configuration 20 
- Radio Bearer Admission Control, to configure DRB admission control such as reject or release may be applied  21 
- Split bearer and PDCP duplication control 22

7.6.2.2 CONTROL Service RIC Control Header IE contents 1 
This CONTROL Service RIC Control Header IE has the UE ID IE, the Control Service Style ID, the Control Action 2 
ID IE and the RIC Control Decision IE that indicates whether the RIC accepts or rejects the INDICATION request from 3 
the previous incoming INSERT indication, if any (with matching RAN Call Process ID IE), from the E2 node.  4 
This CONTROL style uses RIC Control Header IE Format 1 (9.2.1.6.1). 5 
7.6.2.3 CONTROL Service RIC Control Message IE contents 6 
This CONTROL Service RIC Control Message IE contains the sequence of RAN parameters, associated with a given 7 
Control Action within this Control Service style, controlled by the near-RT RIC along with the values for these 8 
parameters, as set by the RIC. 9 
This CONTROL style uses RIC Control Message IE Format 1 (9.2.1.7.1). 10 
The supported RAN control actions are as follows.  11

the previous incoming INSERT indication, if any (with matching RAN Call Process ID IE), from the E2 node.  17 
This CONTROL style uses RIC Control Header IE Format 1 (9.2.1.6.1). 18

parameters, as set by the RIC.  22

7.7 Supported RIC POLICY Services 1 
7.7.1 POLICY Service style list 2 
RIC Style Type Style Name Style Description 
1 Policy for Radio Bearer 
control 
Used to define a policy for modifying the behaviour of Radio 
Bearer Control (RBC) of call processes for a specific RAN UE 
Group based on cell, slice, UE list and/or QoS 
2 Policy for Radio resource 
allocation control 
Used to define a policy for modifying the behaviour of Radio 
Resource Allocation control of call processes for a specific RAN 
UE Group based on cell, slice, UE list and/or QoS 
3 Policy for Connected mode 
mobility control  
Used to define a policy for modifying the behaviour of connected 
mode mobility procedure (Handover or Conditional Handover), 
optionally with Dual Active Protocol Stack (DAPS), call processes 
for a specific RAN UE Group based on cell, slice, UE list and/or 
QoS 
4 Policy for Radio access 
control 
Used to define a policy for modifying the behaviour of radio access 
control processes 
5 Policy for Dual connectivity 
(DC) control 
Used to define a policy for modifying the behaviour of dual 
connectivity (DC) call processes for a specific RAN UE Group 
based on cell, slice, UE list and/or QoS 
6 Policy for Carrier Aggregation 
(CA) control 
Used to define a policy for modifying the behaviour of carrier 
aggregation (CA) call processes for a specific RAN UE Group 
based on cell, slice, UE list and/or QoS 
7 Policy for Idle mode mobility 
control 
Used to define a policy for modifying the behaviour of idle mode 
configuration call processes for a specific RAN UE Group based 
on cell, slice and/or UE list. 
 3 
Each of the POLICY Service Styles 1-7 listed above are supported using the following common features: 4 
• Event Trigger: POLICY service is initiated by either Event Trigger style 1: Conditional Message Arrival  or 5 
Event Trigger style 2: Call process breakpoint. 6 
• A ction ID : The index ID for the individual action under a given POLICY Service style. 7 
• A ction Name: Indicates the functionality of the E2 node which is controlled by Near -RT RIC 8 
• A ction Description : Describes the action and functionality of the receiving E2 Node. 9 
• A ssociated RAN parameters: Identifies the RAN parameters to be controlled by Near -RT RIC pertaining to the 10 
given Policy action, used to define Policy Condition and RAN Imperative Policy.  11 
All POLICY Service styles use RIC Action Definition IE Format 2 (9.2.1.2.2) which provides the policy conditions and 12 
corresponding Policy Action. All of these factors are defined as a sequence of RAN Parameters assigned according to a 13 
given Policy Style and Policy Action where: 14 
- Policy Action ID is a Policy specific identifier of a specific Action for a specific Policy style. 15 
- Policy Condition is a Policy specific condition to select a specific Policy Action. Policy Condition is described in 16 
terms of a list of test conditions concerning UE and E2 Node information selection criteria using RAN 17 
Parameters defined with a Conditional Criteria Definition. Default RAN behaviour is to be applied to any UE 18 
when none of the Policy conditions are met. 19 
- Policy Action is encoded in terms of a list of specific RAN Parameters and shall be applied to any UE within a 20 
given RAN UE Group that meets a specific Policy Condition.   21 
The details of the individual POLICY Service Styles and specific Policy Actions are provided in subsequent sections.  22

8 RAN Parameter assignments 1 
8.1 RAN parameters for Event Trigger 2 
8.1.1 Approach and Common RAN Parameters 3 
The RAN parameters associated with each control action being controlled by Near -RT RIC described in Section 7.3 are 4 
listed.  Each RAN parameter belongs to one of the following value types: 5 
• ELEMENT: a singleton variable, which does not have any other associated RAN parameters.  6 
• STRUCTURE: a sequence of RAN parameters, each of which can be either an ELEMENT or a STRUCTURE 7 
or a LIST 8 
• LIST: a list of STRUCTURES, where each STRUCTURE is as defined above. The sequence of RAN parameters 9 
is the same across all the STRUCTURES within the list. 10 
The corresponding 3GPP standard definitions of these RAN parameters (if available) are referenced in the tables belo w 11 
under the “RAN Parameter Definition” column. These RAN parameters having 3GPP standard definitions are not freshly 12 
defined or redefined here.  13 
Note that only those RAN parameters identified as ELEMENT are subject to test conditions by the RIC in the “Eve nt 14 
Trigger Definition”.  15 
Note that a RAN parameter may be associated with as a key where its corresponding Key Flag  is set to “TRUE”. These 16 
RAN parameters serve as a reference to other RAN parameters within a structure that may be a part of LIST to enable 17 
the E2 Node interpret the scope of RAN parameters that are controlled by Near -RT RIC. 18 
If the “key flag” is specified in the RIC Event Trigger Definition, then the RAN parameters corresponding to “that specific 19 
itemized structure” in the list indexed by the “key flag” are subject to test condition, but if the “key flag” is not mentioned 20 
in the RIC Event Trigger Definition, then the RAN parameters corresponding to “any itemized structure” within the list 21 
are subject to test condition.  22 
For e.g., The ‘QFI’ can be considered a ‘key parameter’ to identify a QoS flow among the list of flows in a UE -specific 23 
PDU session. If the QFI parameter is NOT mentioned and the RIC subscribes to an event pertaining to 5QI 8, then “any 24 
QoS flow” in the list of flows of a PDU se ssion for the UE that matches the condition of 5QI being equal to 8 would be 25 
covered by this event trigger definition. On the other hand, if the QFI parameter is mentioned in the event trigger 26 
definition, then only that specific QoS flow pertaining to the indicated QFI within the list is covered.   27 
The RAN Parameters pertaining to “Event Trigger” that are used across multiple service styles are also listed here.  28

8.3 RAN parameters for INSERT services 3 
8.3.1 Approach 4 
The RAN parameters associated with each insert indication being requested by E2 node described in Section 7.5 are listed.  5 
Each RAN parameter belongs to one of the following value types: 6 
• ELEMENT: a singleton variable, which does not have any other associated RAN parameters.  7 
• STRUCTURE: a sequence of RAN parameters, each of which can be either an ELEMENT or a STRUCTURE 8 
or a LIST 9 
• LIST: a list of STRUCTURES, where each STRUCTURE is as defined above. The sequence of RAN parameters 10 
is the same across all the STRUCTURES within the list. 11 
The corresponding 3GPP standard definitions of these RAN parameters (if available) are referenced in the tables below 12 
under the “RAN Parameter Definition” column. These RAN parameters having 3GPP standard definitions are not freshly 13 
defined or redefined here.  14 
Note that a RAN parameter may be associated with as a key where its corresponding Key Flag  is set to “TRUE”. These 15 
RAN parameters serve as a reference to other RAN parameters within a structure that is part of a list to enable the near -16 
RT RIC to interpret the scope of RAN parameters that are requested to be controlled by the E2 node.  17

8.3.9.2 E2 Node Context Information 1 
The associated RAN parameters are given in Section 8.1.1.11. 2 
8.3.10 Indication Semantics Description for interpretation by the RIC 3 
The E2 node requests the near-RT RIC for the following services as far as the radio bearer Control request is concerned.  4 
(a) In the RIC Indication Header IE, the E2 node indicates the Insert Indication ID, that is associated with the Insert 5 
Service Style ID for the radio bearer control request, along with the UE ID, so as to enable the RIC to interpret 6 
which Insert Indication service pertaining to which UE is being requested by the E2 node.  7 
(b) In the RIC Indication Message IE, the E2 node indicates the list of the RAN parameters in the Indication message 8 
that it wants to be controlled by the near-RT RIC. If the E2 node does not provide values for these parameters in 9 
the RIC Indication message IE, then the RIC would set the values for these parameters in the control action sent 10 
via the RIC Control Request message, along with its decision to accept/deny the request raised by the E2 node 11 
(indicated in the RIC Indication Header IE). If the RAN parameter indicate d by the E2 node is an ELEMENT, 12 
the RIC would set the value for the parameter in its RIC Control Request message. If the indicated RAN 13 
parameter is a STRUCTURE but if the E2 node does not list any constitutent RAN parameter of the 14 
STRUCTURE, then the RIC would set the values for all the constitutent RAN parameters of the STRUCTURE. 15 
If the parameter is a LIST, then: 16 
a. If the E2 node also indicates the Key RAN parameter pertaining to the itemized STRUCTURE in the 17 
LIST, then the RIC would set the values for all constituent RAN parameters within the structure, pointed 18 
by the key. 19 
b. If the E2 node does not indicate the Key  RAN parameter pertaining to the itemized STRUCTURE in 20 
the LIST, then the RIC would set the values for all constituent RAN parameters within each itemized 21 
STRUCTURE, whose key RAN parameter is identified by the RIC. 22 
(c) If the E2 node provides values for these parameters in the RIC Indication message IE, then the RIC would set 23 
the values only for those indicated parameters for which it would choose  to replace the values already set by 24 
the E2 node. It also communicates its decision to accept/deny the request raised by the E2 node for the DRB.  25 
(d) Any RAN parameter identified as a key shall always carry a value set by the E2 node, if the E2 node expects 26 
the RIC to control the parameters pertaining to the STRUCTURE pointed by the E2 node. The value of this key 27 
RAN parameter is an index that points to the entire STRUCTURE, and hence the value of the key RAN 28 
parameter cannot be modified by the near-RT RIC. Without indicating the value for the key RAN parameter, 29 
the RIC would not control the parameters associated with the structure indexed by the key. 30 
Note that the RIC can only set the values for those RAN parameters identified as ELEMENT when they are indicated 31 
by the E2 node; however, these RAN parameters can be contained with a STRUCTURE or within an itemized 32 
STRUCTURE in a LIST. Also, if the DRB ID key parameter is not present for any DRB in the RIC Indication 33 
Message IE, then the RIC would discard the RIC Indication message. And the E2 node would have to set values 34 
based on its default radio resource management policies upon time out, and continue with the ongoing call processing. 35 
Hence, indicating the DRB ID  IE for the DRB(s) is a pre -requisite for the RIC to act on the Insert indication via its 36 
RIC Control Request message. 37 
8.4 RAN Parameters for Control Actions 38 
8.4.1 Approach 39 
The RAN parameters associated with each control action being controlled by Near -RT RIC described in Section 7.6 are 40 
listed.  Each RAN parameter belongs to one of the following value types: 41 
• ELEMENT: a singleton variable, which does not have any other associated RAN parameters.  42 
• STRUCTURE: a sequence of RAN parameters, each of which can be either an ELEMENT or a STRUCTURE 43 
or a LIST 44 

ORAN.WG3.E2SM-RC-v01.00 
 
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN ALLIANCE e.V. Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in the Annex ZZZ 
156 
• LIST: a list of STRUCTURES, where each STRUCTURE is as defined above. The sequence of RAN parameters 1 
is the same across all the STRUCTURES within the list. 2 
The corresponding 3GPP standard definitions of these RAN parameters (if available) are referenced in the tables below 3 
under the “RAN Parameter Definition” column. These RAN parameters having 3GPP standard definitions are not freshly 4 
defined or redefined here.  5 
Note that only those RAN parameters identified as ELEMENT are controlled by Near -RT RIC.  6 
Note that a RAN parameter may be associated with as a key where its corresponding Key Flag  is set to “TRUE”. These 7 
RAN parameters serve as a reference to other RAN parameters within a structure that may be a part of LIST to enable the 8 
E2 Node interpret the scope of RAN parameters that are controlled by Near -RT RIC.  9

missing in the RIC Control Request message, the E2 node will send a RIC Control Failure . 15

8.4.2.6 DRB Split Ratio Control 1 
Upon receiving the RIC Control Request message, in the presence of Downlink PDCP Data Split IE, the E2 node shall 2 
split the downlink PDCP traffic between the Master Node and Secondary Node over the X2/Xn interface based on the 3 
recommended ratio. In the presence of Uplink PDCP Data Split Threshold IE, the E2 node shall invoke procedures related 4 
to DRB Split Ratio Control, such as Bearer Context Management, UE Context Management, RRC Message Transfer, etc. 5

8.4.3.6 Slice-level PRB quota 1 
Upon receiving the RIC Control Request message, the E2 node allocates slice- specific PRB quota for the indicated S -2 
NSSAI in terms of the maximum PRB allocation ratio, minimum PRB allocation ratio and dedicated PRB allocation ratio 3 
for the given slice among the available set of PRBs. If the S -NSSAI is missing in the RIC Control Request message, the 4 
E2 node will send a RIC Control Failure. 5

8.4.4.1 Handover Control 4

procedures, such as UE Context Modification , RRC Message Transfer, etc. The E2 node includes the IEs corresponding 8 
to one or more of parameters described below in the related interface messages. If the Target Primary Cell ID IE is 9 
missing in the RIC Control Request message, the E2 node will send a RIC Control Failure message.  10

8.4.4.2 Conditional Handover Control 2 
Upon receiving the RIC Control Request message, in the case of Xn/X2 or NG or inter -RAT conditional handovers, the 3 
E2 node shall invoke procedures, such as  Handover Preparation related to UE Mobility Management, Bearer Context 4 
Modification, UE Context Modification, RRC Message Transfer, etc. involving the candidate target cells (note that there 5 
is only one Handover Preparation in the case of NG or inter-RAT handovers). In the case of intra-gNB or F1 conditional 6 
handover, the E2 node shall invoke procedures,  such as UE Context Modification , RRC Message Transfer, etc. The E2 7 
node includes the IEs corresponding to one or more of parameters described below in the related interface messages. If 8 
the Target Cell IE is missing in the RIC Control Request message, the E2 node will send a RIC Control Failure message. 9

8.4.6.3 PSCell Change control for Secondary Cell Group 3 
Upon receiving the RIC Control Request message, in the case of intra- SN PSCell change, the E2 node shall invoke 4 
procedures related to PSCell Change Control, such as Dual Connectivity Secondary Node Modification , UE Context 5 
Modification, RRC Message Transfer, etc. In the case of inter -SN PSCell change, the E2 node shall invoke procedures 6 
such as Dual Connectivity Secondary Node Release (MN/SN-initiated) or SN Change (only SN-initiated), Bearer Context 7 
Modification, UE Context Modification, RRC Message Transfer, etc. The E2 node then includes the IEs corresponding to 8 
one or more of parameters described below in the related interface messages.  9

8.5 RAN parameters for POLICY services 6 
8.5.1 Approach 7 
The RAN parameters associated with each control action being controlled by Near -RT RIC described in Section 7.6 are 8 
listed.  Each RAN parameter belongs to one of the following value types: 9 
- ELEMENT: a singleton variable, which does not have any other associated RAN parameters. 10 
- STRUCTURE: a sequence of RAN parameters, each of which can be either an ELEMENT or a STRUCTURE or 11 
a LIST 12 
- LIST: a list of STRUCTURES, where each STRUCTURE is as defined above. The sequence of RAN par ameters 13 
is the same across all the STRUCTURES within the list. 14 
The corresponding 3GPP standard definitions of these RAN parameters (if available) are referenced in the tables below 15 
under the “RAN Parameter Definition” column. These RAN parameters having 3GPP standard definitions are not freshly 16 
defined or redefined here.  17 
Note that only those RAN parameters identified as ELEMENT are controlled by Near -RT RIC whose definitions are 18 
defined on their corresponding “RAN Parameter definition”.  19 
Note that a RAN pa rameter may be associated with as a key where its corresponding Key Flag  is set to “TRUE”. These 20 
RAN parameters serve as a reference to other RAN parameters within a structure that may be a part of LIST to enable the 21 
E2 Node interpret the scope of RAN parameters that are controlled by Near-RT RIC.  22 
There are two types of E2 policies: 23 
(i) Control action policy: In this type, the near-RT RIC tells the E2 node on the specific per-UE control action 24 
that needs to be performed, upon meeting a given policy condition for a given UE or a group of UEs, for a 25 
given cell and/or for a given E2 node. This policy type is descriptive in nature. The control action is defined 26 
with respect to individual UEs and UE-specific bearers, flows, PDU sessions, etc.  27 

ORAN.WG3.E2SM-RC-v01.00 
 
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN ALLIANCE e.V. Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in the Annex ZZZ 
200 
(ii) OFFSET policy: In this type, the near-RT RIC offers a generic prescriptive guidance to the E2 node on how 1 
it shall deviate from default behaviour via the application of offset parameters provided in the POLICY 2 
Action IE. Different POLICY Action IEs are associated with different POLICY conditions described in 3 
terms of UE and E2 Node characteristics. 4 
The common set of RAN Parameters that can be used across all POLICY service styles is given in the table below.  5

9.2.1.2.2 E2SM-RC Action Definition Format 2: Policy with Conditions 13 
The E2SM-RC Action Definition IE Format 2 supports a POLICY services encoded as a list of Policy Conditions, each 14 
with a Policy Condition definition described using Conditional Criteria Definition IE in terms of a list of RAN 15 
parameters with test conditions and a Policy Action IE command described in terms of a list of RAN parameters. The 16 
meaning of the RAN Parameter ID/Value pairs for each list is defined in Section 8.5. 17

9.3 Information Element definitions 4 
9.3.1 General 5 
When specifying information elements which are to be represented by bit strings, if not otherwise specifically stated in 6 
the semantics description of the concerned IE or elsewhere, the following principle applies with regards to the ordering 7 
of bits: 8 
- The first bit (leftmost bit) contains the most significant bit (MSB); 9 
- The last bit (rightmost bit) contains the least significant bit (LSB); 10 
- When importing bit strings from other specifications, the first bit of the bit string contains the first bit of the 11 
concerned information. 12 

ORAN.WG3.E2SM-RC-v01.00 
 
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN ALLIANCE e.V. Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in the Annex ZZZ 
234

9.3.11 RAN Parameter Value Type 1 
This IE specifies the RAN parameters controlled by the RIC. The parameters can be individual elements, or structures 2 
containing constituent elements or a list of structures. The parameters and their types are given in Section 8.4.  3 
IE/Group Name Presence Range IE type and 
reference 
Semantics description 
CHOICE RAN Parameter 
Value Type 
M  
 
A RAN Parameter can either be an 
ELEMENT or a STRUCTURE or a LIST. 
 >ELEMENT with Key Flag 
TRUE

9.4 Information Element Abstract Syntax (with ASN.1) 4 
9.4.1 General 5 
E2SM-RC ASN.1 definition conforms to ITU-T Rec. X.680 [5] and ITU-T Rec. X.681 [6]. 6 
Sub clause  9.4.2 presents the Abstract Syntax of the E2SM information elements to be carried  within the E2AP [3] 7 
protocol messages with ASN.1. In case there is contradiction between the ASN.1 definition in this sub clause  and the 8 
tabular format in sub clause 9.2 and 9.3, the ASN.1 shall take precedence, except for the definition of conditions for the 9 
presence of conditional elements, in which the tabular format shall take precedence. 10 
If an E2SM information element carried as an OCTET STRING in an E2AP [3] message that is not constructed as defined 11 
above is received, this shall be considered as Abstract Syntax Error, and the message shall be handled as defined for 12 
Abstract Syntax Error in clause 9. 13

AGREES TO THE TERMS OF THIS AGREEMENT. 3 
This O-RAN Adopter License Agreement (the “Agreement”) is made by and between the O -RAN Alliance and the 4 
entity that downloads, uses or otherwise accesses any O-RAN Specification, including its Affiliates (the “Adopter”). 5 
This is a license agreement for entities who wish to adopt any O-RAN Specification. 6 
Section 1: DEFINITIONS 7 
1.1 “Affiliate” means an entity that directly or indirectly controls, is controlled by, or is under common control with 8 
another entity, so long as such control exists. For the purpose of this Section, “Control” means beneficial ownership of 9 
fifty (50%) percent or more of the voting stock or equity in an entity. 10 
1.2 “Compliant Implementation” means any system, device, method or operation (whether implemented in hardware, 11 
software or combinations thereof) that fully conforms to a Final Specification. 12 
1.3 “Adopter(s)” means all entities, who are not Members, Contributors or Academic Contributors, including their 13 
Affiliates, who wish to download, use or otherwise access O-RAN Specifications. 14 
1.4 “Minor Update” means an update or revision to an O-RAN Specification published by O-RAN Alliance that does 15 
not add any significant new features or functionality and remains interoperable with the prior version of an O -RAN 16 
Specification. The term “O-RAN Specifications” includes Minor Updates. 17 
1.5 “Necessary Claims” means those claims of all present and future patents and patent applications, other than design 18 
patents and design registrations, throughout the world, which (i) are owned or otherwise licensable by a Member, 19 
Contributor or Academic Contributor during the term of its Member, Contributor or Academic Contributorship; (ii) 20 
such Member, Contributor or Academic Contributor has the right to grant a license without the payment of 21 
consideration to a third party; and (iii) are necessarily infringed by a Compliant Implementation (without considering 22 
any Contributions not included in the Final Specification). A claim is necessarily infringed only when it is not possible 23 
on technical (but not commercial) grounds, taking into account normal technical practice and the state of the art 24 
generally available at the date any Final Specification was published by the O -RAN Alliance or the date the patent 25 
claim first came into existence, whichever last occurred, to make, sell, lease, otherwise dispose of, repair, use or operate 26 
a Compliant Implementation without infringing that claim. For the avoidance of doubt in exceptional cases where a 27 
Final Specification can only be implemented by technical solutions, all of which infringe patent claims, all suc h patent 28 
claims shall be considered Necessary Claims. 29 
1.6 “Defensive Suspension” means for the purposes of any license grant pursuant to Section 3, Member, Contributor, 30 
Academic Contributor, Adopter, or any of their Affiliates, may have the discretion to i nclude in their license a term 31 
allowing the licensor to suspend the license against a licensee who brings a patent infringement suit against the 32 
licensing Member, Contributor, Academic Contributor, Adopter, or any of their Affiliates.  33
